The standard approach for JSSP heuristics:\n\n1. **List scheduling**: Maintain a priority queue of "available" operations (operations whose predecessor in the same job has been completed). For medium instances, I\'ll do tabu search.\n\nThe standard tabu search for JSSP:\n1. Represent schedule as a list of operation sequences on each machine\n2. Compute critical path\n3. Neighbor = swap two consecutive operations on the same machine that are both on the critical path\n4. Tabu = recently performed swaps\n\nFor simplicity, I\'ll implement a simpler local search: for each pair of consecutive operations on the same machine, try swapping and accept if it improves.\n\nLet me implement this as part of the tabu search.\n\nActually, let me think about what data structures I need for the local search:\n\nI need to maintain:\n- `machineOrder[m]`: order of jobs on machine m\n- `start[j][p]`: start time of operation (j,p)\n- `makespan`\n\nAfter swapping two consecutive ops on machine m, I need to recompute start times. This can be done efficiently by only updating affected parts.\n\nFor simplicity, I\'ll recompute the full schedule from the machine orders after each swap.\n\nGiven machine orders, computing start times is straightforward:\n```\nFor each machine m, in order machineOrder[m]:\n    For each op (j, pos) on m:\n        start[j][pos] = max(machFree[m], jobReady[j])\n        machFree[m] = start[j][pos] + dur\n        jobReady[j] = machFree[m]\n```\n\nBut this doesn\'t work directly because jobs might have ops on different machines, creating dependencies.\n\nI need to compute a topological sort of all operations and then assign start times.\n\nAlternatively, I can use the following approach:\n- Operations have two types of edges: job-order edges and machine-order edges\n- Compute longest path from source for each operation\n\nThis is the critical path calculation and is O(n) if done in topological order.\n\nLet me implement this:\n\n```cpp\nvector<vector<int>> computeStartTimes(\n    const vector<vector<int>>& machOrder,\n    const vector<vector<int>>& jobMachine,\n    const vector<vector<int>>& jobDuration\n) {\n    int J = jobMachine.size();\n    int M = machOrder.size(); // assumed\n    \n    // For each op, earliest start = max(pred_job start + pred_job dur, pred_mach start + pred_mach dur)\n    // We need to process in topological order\n    \n    // Build predecessor info\n    // For op (j, p): job pred = (j, p-1), mach pred = previous op in machOrder[m]\n    \n    // machPos[j][p] = position of (j,p) in machOrder[m]\n    // prev in machine order\n    vector<vector<int>> machPrev(J); Let me use a simpler but still correct approach:\n\nSince the job order is fixed, I can process ops in a way that respects both constraints:\n\nFor each operation (j, p):\n- It depends on (j, p-1) [job predecessor]\n- It depends on the op just before it in machine order [machine predecessor]\n\nI can compute start times using a modified topological sort.\n\nActually, the simplest correct approach for recomputing start times given machine orders is:\n\n```\nrepeat:\n    for each machine m:\n        for each op in machOrder[m] in order:\n            early_start = max(job_pred_end, mach_pred_end)\n            update start time\nuntil no changes\n```\n\nThis converges in at most M iterations.\n\nFor the tabu search, let me use a different representation. Time limit: adaptive based on problem size\n\nFor the schedule recomputation from machine orders, I\'ll use the forward pass:\n\nGiven machineOrder[m] (list of (job, opIdx) pairs in machine order), compute start times:\n\n```\nfor each op, compute:\n  earliest[j][p] = max(earliest[j][p-1] + dur[j][p-1], machPred end time)\n```\n\nI need to process in an order such that when I compute earliest[j][p], both earliest[j][p-1] and machPred have been computed.\n\nThis is equivalent to a topological sort of the DAG.\n\nFor JSSP with given machine orders, the DAG is acyclic (assuming the machine orders are consistent), and we can compute it with a topological sort.\n\nHere\'s a simpler way: since job ops are already ordered, I can use the following:\n\n```\nFor each machine m:\n    Maintain pointer to next op in machOrder[m]\n\nProcess all ops in order of earliest possible start time:\n    For each op (j, p):\n        earliest start = max(job pred end, mach pred end)\n        if both job pred and mach pred have been scheduled:\n            schedule this op\n```\n\nThis is essentially the same as the greedy scheduler but with fixed machine orders!\n\nSo I can reuse my greedy scheduler with a modified selection: instead of MWKR, select the next op in the fixed machine order.\n\nLet me implement this:\n\n```cpp\nint computeMakespan(\n    const vector<vector<pair<int,int>>>& machOrder, // machOrder[m] = [(job,opIdx),...]\n    ...\n) {\n    // machNext[m]: index in machOrder[m] of next op to schedule\n    vector<int> machNext(M, 0);\n    vector<int> machFree(M, 0);\n    vector<int> jobReady(J, 0); // when job\'s current op can start\n    \n    // For each op, track if it\'s scheduled\n    // ... same simulation as before but with fixed order\n    \n    int total = ...; // total ops\n    \n    // We need to process ops in dependency order\n    // Use a topological sort approach\n    \n    // For each machine m, the "ready" op is machOrder[m][machNext[m]]\n    // It can be scheduled when:\n    //   1. The machine is free (machFree[m] satisfied)\n    //   2. The job predecessor is done (jobReady[j][p-1] satisfied)\n    \n    // This is the same as my greedy scheduler!\n    // Just the selection is different: when multiple ops are available on a machine,\n    // we must take the one that comes first in machOrder\n    \n    // So actually, for a fixed machine order:\n    // We process machOrder[m][0] first, then machOrder[m][1], etc. for each machine\n    // The earliest start time for machOrder[m][k] = max(machFree[m] after k-1 ops, jobPredEnd[j][p])\n    // But machFree after k-1 ops depends on when those ops were scheduled...\n    \n    // Let\'s use iterative computation:\n    vector<vector<int>> startTime(J);\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) startTime[j].resize(jobMachine[j].size(), 0);\n    \n    // Compute in topological order\n    // Nodes: (j, p) with edges: (j, p-1) -> (j, p) and machPred(j, p) -> (j, p)\n    \n    // Using Kahn\'s algorithm:\n    // In-degree of (j,p):\n    //   1 if p==0 and no mach pred\n    //   1 if p==0 and has mach pred (from mach pred)\n    //   1 if p>0 and no mach pred (from job pred)\n    //   2 if p>0 and has mach pred\n    \n    // Actually, let me just use a simple approach:\n    // Iterate over ops in a valid order and compute start times\n    \n    // Since we know the machine orders and job orders,\n    // we can compute earliest start times by:\n    // for op (j, p) at position k in machOrder[m]:\n    //   start[j][p] = max(start[j][p-1] + dur[j][p-1], // job constraint\n    //                     start of machOrder[m][k-1] + dur of that op) // machine constraint\n    \n    // But the circular dependency: start[j][p] depends on start of mach pred,\n    // which might depend on start[j\'][p\'] which depends on ...\n    // This is not circular if the machine order doesn\'t create cycles.\n    \n    // For acyclic schedules, we can compute by repeatedly updating until stable.\n    // Max iterations = number of ops (Bellman-Ford)\n    \n    // For efficiency, use topological order:\n    \n    // Build adjacency list\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\nLet me just implement the Bellman-Ford style update, which is correct for acyclic schedules:\n\n```cpp\n// Given machine orders, compute earliest start times\nvoid updateSchedule(\n    const vector<vector<pair<int,int>>>& machOrder,\n    vector<vector<int>>& start\n) {\n    bool changed = true;\n    while(changed) {\n        changed = false;\n        for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n            for(int p=0;p<(int)jobMachine[j].size();p++) {\n                int es = 0;\n                if(p > 0) es = max(es, start[j][p-1] + jobDuration[j][p-1]);\n                // machine predecessor\n                int m = jobMachine[j][p];\n                // Find position of (j,p) in machOrder[m]\n                // Need machPos[j][p] precomputed\n                // ...\n                int newStart = es;\n                if(newStart > start[j][p]) {\n                    start[j][p] = newStart;\n                    changed = true;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis requires knowing the machine predecessor for each operation, which depends on the machine order.\n\nLet me precompute: `machPred[j][p]` = the op just before (j,p) in machOrder[m].\n\nOK I think I\'m overcomplicating this. Let me use a cleaner approach.\n\nFor the tabu search, I\'ll represent the solution as machine operation orders and recompute start times using a topological sort each time.\n\nHere\'s a clean implementation:\n\n```cpp\nstruct JSP {\n    int J, M;\n    vector<vector<int>> machine; // machine[j][p]\n    vector<vector<int>> duration; // duration[j][p]\n    \n    // Solution representation\n    struct Solution {\n        vector<vector<pair<int,int>>> machOrder; // machOrder[m] = list of (j,p)\n        vector<vector<int>> start; // start[j][p]\n        int makespan;\n    };\n    \n    // Compute start times given machine orders\n    // Returns makespan\n    int computeStartTimes(Solution& sol) {\n        // For each op, machPredIdx[m][k] = index k-1 (or -1 for first)\n        // Precompute machPos[j][p] = position in machOrder[machine[j][p]]\n        \n        vector<vector<int>> machPos(J);\n        for(int j=0;j<J;j++) machPos[j].resize(machine[j].size());\n        \n        for(int m=0;m<M;m++) {\n            for(int k=0;k<(int)sol.machOrder[m].size();k++) {\n                auto [j,p] = sol.machOrder[m][k];\n                machPos[j][p] = k;\n            }\n        }\n        \n        // Compute start times using topological sort (Kahn\'s algorithm)\n        // Edges: job order + machine order\n        \n        int n = 0; // total ops\n        for(int j=0;j<J;j++) n += machine[j].size();\n        \n        // Map (j,p) to index\n        vector<int> opOffset(J);\n        opOffset[0] = 0;\n        for(int j=1;j<J;j++) opOffset[j] = opOffset[j-1] + machine[j-1].size();\n        auto opIdx = [&](int j, int p) { return opOffset[j] + p; };\n        \n        vector<int> inDeg(n, 0);\n        vector<vector<int>> succ(n);\n        \n        for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n            for(int p=0;p<(int)machine[j].size();p++) {\n                // Job order edge: (j,p-1) -> (j,p)\n                if(p > 0) {\n                    succ[opIdx(j,p-1)].push_back(opIdx(j,p));\n                    inDeg[opIdx(j,p)]++;\n                }\n                // Machine order edge: prev in machOrder -> (j,p)\n                int m = machine[j][p];\n                int k = machPos[j][p];\n                if(k > 0) {\n                    auto [pj,pp] = sol.machOrder[m][k-1];\n                    succ[opIdx(pj,pp)].push_back(opIdx(j,p));\n                    inDeg[opIdx(j,p)]++;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        \n        // Kahn\'s algorithm with earliest start time\n        sol.start.resize(J);\n        for(int j=0;j<J;j++) sol.start[j].resize(machine[j].size(), 0);\n        \n        queue<int> q;\n        for(int i=0;i<n;i++) if(inDeg[i]==0) q.push(i);\n        \n        int makespan = 0;\n        while(!q.empty()) {\n            int u = q.front(); q.pop();\n            // Decode u\n            // Find j, p from opIdx\n            // Binary search opOffset\n            int j = upper_bound(opOffset.begin(), opOffset.end(), u) - opOffset.begin() - 1;\n            int p = u - opOffset[j];\n            \n            int endTime = sol.start[j][p] + duration[j][p];\n            makespan = max(makespan, endTime);\n            \n            for(int v : succ[u]) {\n                // Decode v\n                int vj = upper_bound(opOffset.begin(), opOffset.end(), v) - opOffset.begin() - 1;\n                int vp = v - opOffset[vj];\n                sol.start[vj][vp] = max(sol.start[vj][vp], endTime);\n                if(--inDeg[v] == 0) q.push(v);\n            }\n        }\n        \n        sol.makespan = makespan;\n        return makespan;\n    }\n};\n```\n\nThis is O(n) for each schedule computation. Each tabu search step does O(1) swaps and one schedule computation, so O(n) per step.\n\nFor a tabu search with T_max iterations on a problem with n ops, total time is O(T_max * n).\n\nFor n=50k and T_max=1000, that\'s 50M operations - feasible.\n\nBut for large instances we want fewer iterations, and for small instances we want more.\n\nLet me now put together the complete solution:\n\n1. Parse input\n2. Compute initial solution with MWKR greedy\n3. Extract machine orders from greedy solution\n4. Run tabu search with time limit (based on problem size)\n5. Output best solution\n\nFor the tabu search neighborhood:\n- Find critical path (longest path in DAG)\n- For each arc (u, v) on critical path where u and v are on the same machine (consecutive in machine order):\n  - Swap u and v in machine order\n  - This creates a new schedule\n  - Check makespan\n  - If improving, accept\n  - Keep as best even if not improving (tabu search)\n\nThe critical path identification:\n- Compute earliest finish times (forward pass)\n- Compute latest start times (backward pass)\n- Op (j,p) is on critical path if latest_start[j][p] == earliest_start[j][p]\n\nLet me implement this.\n\nActually, given the complexity, let me implement a simpler local search:\n\n**Simplified local search:**\n- For each machine m:\n  - For each consecutive pair (i, i+1) in machOrder[m]:\n    - Try swapping them\n    - If makespan improves, accept and restart\n- Repeat until no improvement\n\nThis is a hill-climbing approach (2-opt on machine orders). Simple but effective for small instances.\n\nFor tabu search: maintain a tabu list of recently swapped pairs and also accept non-improving moves.\n\nLet me implement this with a time budget.\n\nHere\'s my complete plan for the code:\n\n```cpp\n#include <bits/stdc++.h>\nusing namespace std;\n\nint J, M;\nvector<vector<int>> jMachine, jDuration, jStart;\nvector<int> jTotalWork;\nint totalOps;\n\n// Compute start times from machine orders\n// machOrder[m] = list of (job, opIdx) in order on machine m\nint computeSchedule(const vector<vector<pair<int,int>>>& machOrder,\n                    vector<vector<int>>& start) {\n    // Build op indices\n    vector<int> opOff(J+1, 0);\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) opOff[j+1] = opOff[j] + jMachine[j].size();\n    \n    // machPred[j][p] = {pj, pp} or {-1,-1}\n    // From machOrder\n    // machPos[j][p] = position in machOrder[m]\n    vector<vector<int>> machPos(J);\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) machPos[j].resize(jMachine[j].size());\n    \n    for(int m=0;m<M;m++)\n        for(int k=0;k<(int)machOrder[m].size();k++) {\n            auto [j,p] = machOrder[m][k];\n            machPos[j][p] = k;\n        }\n    \n    // Topological sort with Kahn\'s\n    // Edges: job order + machine order\n    int n = opOff[J];\n    vector<int> inDeg(n, 0);\n    vector<vector<int>> succ(n);\n    \n    auto idx = [&](int j, int p) { return opOff[j]+p; };\n    \n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n        for(int p=0;p<(int)jMachine[j].size();p++) {\n            if(p>0) { succ[idx(j,p-1)].push_back(idx(j,p)); inDeg[idx(j,p)]++; }\n            int m = jMachine[j][p];\n            int k = machPos[j][p];\n            if(k>0) {\n                auto [pj,pp] = machOrder[m][k-1];\n                succ[idx(pj,pp)].push_back(idx(j,p));\n                inDeg[idx(j,p)]++;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    start.resize(J);\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) start[j].assign(jMachine[j].size(), 0);\n    \n    queue<int> q;\n    for(int i=0;i<n;i++) if(!inDeg[i]) q.push(i);\n    \n    int ms = 0;\n    while(!q.empty()) {\n        int u = q.front(); q.pop();\n        // decode\n        int j = (int)(upper_bound(opOff.begin(),opOff.end(),u)-opOff.begin())-1;\n        int p = u - opOff[j];\n        int et = start[j][p] + jDuration[j][p];\n        ms = max(ms, et);\n        for(int v : succ[u]) {\n            int vj = (int)(upper_bound(opOff.begin(),opOff.end(),v)-opOff.begin())-1;\n            int vp = v - opOff[vj];\n            start[vj][vp] = max(start[vj][vp], et);\n            if(!--inDeg[v]) q.push(v);\n        }\n    }\n    return ms;\n}\n\n// Extract machine orders from start times\nvector<vector<pair<int,int>>> extractMachOrders(const vector<vector<int>>& start) {\n    vector<vector<pair<int,int>>> machOrder(M);\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++)\n        for(int p=0;p<(int)jMachine[j].size();p++)\n            machOrder[jMachine[j][p]].push_back({start[j][p], {j,p}});\n    // Wait, need to sort by start time\n    // Actually each element should be (startTime, j, p)\n    // Then sort by startTime\n    \n    // Hmm, let me redo:\n    vector<vector<pair<int,int>>> result(M);\n    vector<vector<tuple<int,int,int>>> machOps(M); // (startTime, j, p)\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++)\n        for(int p=0;p<(int)jMachine[j].size();p++)\n            machOps[jMachine[j][p]].push_back({start[j][p], j, p});\n    for(int m=0;m<M;m++) {\n        sort(machOps[m].begin(), machOps[m].end());\n        for(auto [t,j,p] : machOps[m])\n            result[m].push_back({j,p});\n    }\n    return result;\n}\n\n// Greedy MWKR scheduler\nvector<vector<int>> greedySchedule() {\n    vector<int> remWork = jTotalWork;\n    vector<vector<int>> start(J);\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) start[j].resize(jMachine[j].size());\n    \n    vector<int> jobNext(J, 0);\n    vector<int> jobReady(J, 0);\n    vector<int> machFree(M, 0);\n    \n    for(int scheduled=0; scheduled<totalOps; ) {\n        // Find minimum time t\n        int t = INT_MAX;\n        for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n            if(jobNext[j] >= (int)jMachine[j].size()) continue;\n            int m = jMachine[j][jobNext[j]];\n            t = min(t, max(machFree[m], jobReady[j]));\n        }\n        \n        // Collect candidates at time t, sorted by remWork desc\n        vector<pair<int,int>> cands;\n        for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n            if(jobNext[j] >= (int)jMachine[j].size()) continue;\n            int m = jMachine[j][jobNext[j]];\n            if(max(machFree[m], jobReady[j]) == t)\n                cands.push_back({remWork[j], j});\n        }\n        sort(cands.begin(), cands.end(), greater<>());\n        \n        set<int> usedM;\n        for(auto [rw,j] : cands) {\n            int p = jobNext[j];\n            int m = jMachine[j][p];\n            if(usedM.count(m)) continue;\n            usedM.insert(m);\n            int dur = jDuration[j][p];\n            start[j][p] = t;\n            machFree[m] = t+dur;\n            jobReady[j] = t+dur;\n            remWork[j] -= dur;\n            jobNext[j]++;\n            scheduled++;\n        }\n    }\n    return start;\n}\n\nint main() {\n    // Read input\n    cin >> J >> M;\n    jMachine.resize(J); Identify all machine arcs (consecutive ops on same machine) where both are on the critical path\n2. Try swapping each such pair\n3. Evaluate new schedule\n4. Best improvement wins\n\nThis is the standard N1 neighborhood from Nowicki & Smutnicki.\n\nFor the code, I need to:\n1. Run forward pass to get EST\n2. Run backward pass to get LST\n3. That\'s fast enough for many iterations.\n\nLet me implement the critical path local search.\n\nOK, I think I\'ve been overthinking this. Let me just write the code. Here\'s my final approach:\n\n**For all instances:**\n1. MWKR greedy scheduling\n\n**For small/medium instances (time permitting):**\n2. Local search:\n   a. Extract machine orders from current schedule\n   b. Compute critical path\n   c. Find critical machine arcs (consecutive ops on same machine, both on CP)\n   d. Try swapping each critical arc\n   e. I\'ll use a time-based termination.\n\nHere\'s my complete implementation:\n\n```cpp\n#include <bits/stdc++.h>\nusing namespace std;\n\nstatic int J, M, nOps;\nstatic vector<vector<int>> jMach, jDur;\nstatic vector<int> jTotWork;\nstatic vector<int> opOff; // opOff[j] = start index of job j\'s ops in flat array\n\nstatic int opId(int j, int p) { return opOff[j] + p; }\nstatic pair<int,int> decodeOp(int id) {\n    // binary search\n    int j = (int)(upper_bound(opOff.begin(), opOff.end(), id) - opOff.begin()) - 1;\n    return {j, id - opOff[j]};\n}\n\n// Evaluate schedule given machine orders\n// mo[m] = list of (j,p) in order on machine m\n// Returns makespan, fills start times and optionally LST for critical path analysis\nstruct EvalResult {\n    int makespan;\n    vector<int> est; // earliest start time [opId]\n    vector<int> lst; // latest start time [opId]\n    bool hasCycle;\n};\n\nEvalResult evaluate(\n    const vector<vector<pair<int,int>>>& mo,\n    bool computeLST = false\n) {\n    EvalResult res;\n    res.makespan = 0;\n    res.hasCycle = false;\n    \n    // Build machine predecessor map\n    // machPredId[id] = id of machine predecessor (-1 if none)\n    // machSuccId[id] = id of machine successor (-1 if none)\n    vector<int> machPredId(nOps, -1);\n    vector<int> machSuccId(nOps, -1);\n    \n    for(int m = 0; m < M; m++) {\n        for(int k = 1; k < (int)mo[m].size(); k++) {\n            auto [j, p] = mo[m][k];\n            auto [pj, pp] = mo[m][k-1];\n            machPredId[opId(j,p)] = opId(pj,pp);\n            machSuccId[opId(pj,pp)] = opId(j,p);\n        }\n    }\n    \n    // Forward pass: compute EST\n    // In-degree for topological sort\n    vector<int> inDeg(nOps, 0);\n    vector<vector<int>> succ(nOps);\n    \n    for(int j = 0; j < J; j++) {\n        int sz = jMach[j].size();\n        for(int p = 0; p < sz; p++) {\n            int u = opId(j, p);\n            if(p > 0) {\n                int v = opId(j, p-1);\n                // edge v -> u\n                succ[v].push_back(u);\n                inDeg[u]++;\n            }\n            if(machPredId[u] >= 0) {\n                int v = machPredId[u];\n                succ[v].push_back(u);\n                inDeg[u]++;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    res.est.assign(nOps, 0);\n    queue<int> q;\n    for(int i = 0; i < nOps; i++)\n        if(!inDeg[i]) q.push(i);\n    \n    int cnt = 0;\n    while(!q.empty()) {\n        int u = q.front(); q.pop();\n        cnt++;\n        auto [j, p] = decodeOp(u);\n        int et = res.est[u] + jDur[j][p];\n        res.makespan = max(res.makespan, et);\n        for(int v : succ[u]) {\n            res.est[v] = max(res.est[v], et);\n            if(!--inDeg[v]) q.push(v);\n        }\n    }\n    \n    if(cnt < nOps) {\n        res.hasCycle = true;\n        return res;\n    }\n    \n    if(computeLST) {\n        // Build predecessor lists for backward pass\n        vector<vector<int>> pred(nOps);\n        for(int u = 0; u < nOps; u++)\n            for(int v : succ[u])\n                pred[v].push_back(u);\n        \n        // Backward pass: compute LST\n        res.lst.assign(nOps, res.makespan);\n        // LST[u] = min(LST[v] for v in succ) - dur[u]\n        // For sinks: LST[u] = makespan - dur[u]\n        \n        // Process in reverse topological order\n        // Use out-degree: process nodes with 0 out-degree first\n        vector<int> outDeg(nOps, 0);\n        for(int u = 0; u < nOps; u++)\n            outDeg[u] = succ[u].size();\n        \n        queue<int> rq;\n        for(int i = 0; i < nOps; i++)\n            if(!outDeg[i]) rq.push(i);\n        \n        while(!rq.empty()) {\n            int v = rq.front(); rq.pop();\n            auto [j, p] = decodeOp(v);\n            // Initialize LST[v]\n            // LST[v] starts at makespan - dur[v], limited by successors\n            // Actually initialized above as makespan, need to adjust:\n            // If v is a sink, lst[v] = makespan - dur[v]\n            // Otherwise, lst[v] = min(lst[succ] - 0) - dur[v]... hmm\n            \n            // Wait, LST is the latest START time, not finish time.\n            // LFT[v] = min(LST[succ[v]] for all succ) if succ non-empty, else makespan\n            // LST[v] = LFT[v] - dur[v]\n            \n            // Let me use LFT instead:\n            // lft[v] = min(lst[u] for u in succ[v]) if succ non-empty, else makespan\n            // lst[v] = lft[v] - dur[v]\n            // ...\n        }\n        \n        // Simpler: just compute backwards\n        // res.lst is "latest finish time" for this computation\n        // Then LST = lft - dur\n        \n        // Let me redefine: lft[v] = latest finish time\n        vector<int> lft(nOps, res.makespan);\n        // Process in reverse topological order\n        // Build reverse topological order from forward pass\n        // I need the topological order stored during forward pass\n        // Let me redo:\n        \n        // Actually, the simplest correct approach:\n        // Run another topological sort on the reversed graph\n        vector<int> revInDeg(nOps, 0);\n        vector<vector<int>> revSucc(nOps); // reverse edges\n        for(int u = 0; u < nOps; u++)\n            for(int v : succ[u]) {\n                revSucc[v].push_back(u);\n                revInDeg[u]++;\n            }\n        // Wait, that\'s just pred!\n        // revSucc[v] = pred[v]\n        // In reverse graph: edges go from v to u for each u->v original edge\n        // "in-degree" in reverse graph = out-degree in original\n        \n        // Process sinks first (out-degree 0 in original = in-degree 0 in reverse)\n        // ...\n        \n        // OK let me just use the already computed succ and reverse-process:\n        // Process in reverse topological order (which we can get by reversing the topological order from forward pass)\n        \n        // I\'ll store topological order during forward pass\n    }\n    \n    return res;\n}\n```\n\nThis is getting really verbose. Let me simplify by combining the forward and backward passes and storing the topological order.\n\nLet me restructure the evaluation function:\n\n```cpp\nint evaluate(\n    const vector<vector<pair<int,int>>>& mo,\n    vector<int>* estOut = nullptr,  // earliest start times\n    vector<int>* lstOut = nullptr,  // latest start times\n    vector<int>* machPredOut = nullptr, // machine predecessor ids\n    vector<int>* machSuccOut = nullptr  // machine successor ids\n) {\n    // Build machine pred/succ\n    vector<int> machPred(nOps, -1), machSucc(nOps, -1);\n    for(int m=0;m<M;m++) {\n        for(int k=1;k<(int)mo[m].size();k++) {\n            auto [j,p] = mo[m][k];\n            auto [pj,pp] = mo[m][k-1];\n            machPred[opId(j,p)] = opId(pj,pp);\n            machSucc[opId(pj,pp)] = opId(j,p);\n        }\n    }\n    \n    // Compute EST\n    // jobSucc: opId(j,p) -> opId(j,p+1)\n    // jobPred: opId(j,p) -> opId(j,p-1)\n    \n    vector<int> est(nOps, 0);\n    // Process in job order (job preds before job succs)\n    // For machine preds, we need topological sort\n    \n    // Use Kahn\'s with in-degrees\n    vector<int> inDeg(nOps, 0);\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n        for(int p=1;p<(int)jMach[j].size();p++)\n            inDeg[opId(j,p)]++; // job pred\n        for(int p=0;p<(int)jMach[j].size();p++)\n            if(machPred[opId(j,p)]>=0)\n                inDeg[opId(j,p)]++; // machine pred\n    }\n    \n    // Process order\n    vector<int> topoOrder;\n    topoOrder.reserve(nOps);\n    queue<int> q;\n    for(int i=0;i<nOps;i++) if(!inDeg[i]) q.push(i);\n    \n    while(!q.empty()) {\n        int u = q.front(); q.pop();\n        topoOrder.push_back(u);\n        auto [j,p] = decodeOp(u);\n        int et = est[u] + jDur[j][p];\n        // job successor\n        if(p+1 < (int)jMach[j].size()) {\n            int v = opId(j,p+1);\n            est[v] = max(est[v], et);\n            if(!--inDeg[v]) q.push(v);\n        }\n        // machine successor\n        if(machSucc[u]>=0) {\n            int v = machSucc[u];\n            est[v] = max(est[v], et);\n            if(!--inDeg[v]) q.push(v);\n        }\n    }\n    \n    if((int)topoOrder.size() < nOps) return -1; // cycle\n    \n    int ms = 0;\n    for(int i=0;i<nOps;i++) {\n        auto [j,p] = decodeOp(i);\n        ms = max(ms, est[i]+jDur[j][p]);\n    }\n    \n    if(estOut) *estOut = est;\n    if(machPredOut) *machPredOut = machPred;\n    if(machSuccOut) *machSuccOut = machSucc;\n    \n    if(lstOut) {\n        // Backward pass\n        vector<int>& lft = *lstOut; // reuse for lft first\n        lft.assign(nOps, ms);\n        \n        // Process in reverse topological order\n        for(int i = (int)topoOrder.size()-1; i>=0; i--) {\n            int u = topoOrder[i];\n            auto [j,p] = decodeOp(u);\n            // lft[u] = min(lft[succ]) (already set)\n            // Now update predecessors:\n            int lst_u = lft[u] - jDur[j][p]; // latest start time\n            // job predecessor\n            if(p>0) {\n                int v = opId(j,p-1);\n                auto [vj, vp] = make_pair(j, p-1);\n                lft[v] = min(lft[v], lst_u); // lft[v] <= lst_u\n            }\n            // machine predecessor\n            if(machPred[u]>=0) {\n                int v = machPred[u];\n                auto [vj, vp] = decodeOp(v);\n                lft[v] = min(lft[v], lst_u);\n            }\n        }\n        \n        // Convert lft to lst (latest start time = lft - dur)\n        for(int i=0;i<nOps;i++) {\n            auto [j,p] = decodeOp(i);\n            lft[i] -= jDur[j][p]; // now it\'s lst\n        }\n    }\n    \n    return ms;\n}\n```\n\nWait, the backward pass is wrong. Let me redo:\n\nFor backward pass, we compute LFT (latest finish time) for each op:\n- For sinks (no successors): LFT = makespan\n- For others: LFT[u] = min(LST[v] for all successors v of u)\n  where LST[v] = LFT[v] - dur[v]\n\nProcessing in reverse topological order:\n\n```\nFor each op u in reverse topological order:\n    LFT[u] = makespan (initialized)\n    // But we need to consider successors that have already been processed\n    // In reverse topo order, successors come BEFORE predecessors\n    // So when we process u, all its successors have been processed\n    \n    LST[u] = LFT[u] - dur[u]\n    \n    // Update predecessors of u:\n    // If v -> u (job pred: v = (j, p-1))\n    //   LFT[v] = min(LFT[v], LST[u])\n    // If v -> u (machine pred: v = machPred[u])\n    //   LFT[v] = min(LFT[v], LST[u])\n```\n\nBut this is what I was computing above, just using `lft` instead of `LFT`. Let me check:\n\n```\nlft initialized to ms for all ops\nProcess in reverse topo order:\n    u = topoOrder[i] (in reverse)\n    lst_u = lft[u] - dur[u]\n    For each predecessor v of u:\n        lft[v] = min(lft[v], lst_u)\n```\n\nThis is correct! An op v is on the critical path if est[v] == lft[v] - dur[v] (i.e., EST[v] == LST[v]).\n\nLet me verify with the example:\nJob 0: (M0, dur=3), (M1, dur=2)\nJob 1: (M1, dur=2), (M0, dur=4)\n\nGreedy gives: start[0]=[0,3], start[1]=[0,3]\nMachOrder[0] = [(0,0), (1,1)] (job 0 op 0 first, then job 1 op 1)\nMachOrder[1] = [(1,0), (0,1)] (job 1 op 0 first, then job 0 op 1)\n\nOpIds: opOff = [0, 2], so opId(0,0)=0, opId(0,1)=1, opId(1,0)=2, opId(1,1)=3\n\nEdges:\n- Job order: 0->1 (j=0 ops), 2->3 (j=1 ops)\n- Machine order: \n  - M0: (0,0)=0 before (1,1)=3: edge 0->3\n  - M1: (1,0)=2 before (0,1)=1: edge 2->1\n\nInDeg: [0, 2, 0, 2] (op0: no pred, op1: job pred op0 + mach pred op2, op2: no pred, op3: job pred op2 + mach pred op0)\n\nForward pass:\n- Process 0 (inDeg=0): est[0]=0, et=3, update op1: est[1]=max(0,3)=3, inDeg[1]--, update op3: est[3]=max(0,3)=3, inDeg[3]--\n- Process 2 (inDeg=0): est[2]=0, et=2, update op3: est[3]=max(3,2)=3, inDeg[3]--, update op1: est[1]=max(3,2)=3, inDeg[1]--\n- Process 1 (inDeg=0): est[1]=3, et=5, no successors\n- Process 3 (inDeg=0): est[3]=3, et=7, no successors\n\nMakespan=7. ✓\n\nBackward pass:\nProcess in reverse topo order: [3, 1, 2, 0] or [3, 1, 0, 2] depending on queue order\n\nLet\'s say: [3, 1, 2, 0]\n- lft = [7, 7, 7, 7]\n- Process 3: lst=7-4=3, update pred op2: lft[2]=min(7,3)=3, update pred op0: lft[0]=min(7,3)=3\n- Process 1: lst=7-2=5, update pred op0: lft[0]=min(3,5)=3, update pred op2: lft[2]=min(3,5)=3\n- Process 2: lst=3-2=1... wait, lft[2]=3, so lst=3-2=1; update predecessors of 2: it has no predecessors\n- Process 0: lft[0]=3, lst=3-3=0; update predecessors of 0: it has no predecessors\n\nSo: EST=[0,3,0,3], LST=lft-dur=[3-3=0, 7-2=5, 3-2=1, 7-4=3]\nWait, I need to convert: lft is latest finish time, and after processing we convert to latest start time.\n\nAfter backward pass:\nlft = [3, 7, 3, 7]\nlst = lft - dur = [3-3=0, 7-2=5, 3-2=1, 7-4=3]\n\nCritical path: ops where EST == LST:\n- Op 0: EST=0, LST=0 → on CP ✓\n- Op 1: EST=3, LST=5 → not on CP\n- Op 2: EST=0, LST=1 → not on CP\n- Op 3: EST=3, LST=3 → on CP ✓\n\nCritical path = {op0, op3} = {(0,0), (1,1)}\n\nCritical machine arcs: consecutive pairs on same machine where both are on CP.\n- M0 order: [(0,0), (1,1)] → both on CP → this is a critical arc!\n- M1 order: [(1,0), (0,1)] → (1,0) not on CP, (0,1) not on CP → no critical arc\n\nSo the only critical arc is (0,0) → (1,1) on M0.\n\nIf we swap this arc:\n- M0 order: [(1,1), (0,0)]\n- Now op (1,1) comes before (0,0) on M0\n- But (1,1) has job predecessor (1,0) which must come first!\n- And (0,0) must come before (1,1) in job 1\'s order? No! Job 1\'s order is (1,0) then (1,1).\n- So now M0: [(1,1), (0,0)]\n  - machPred[(0,0)] = (1,1)\n  - machPred[(1,1)] = none\n\nBut (1,1) requires (1,0) to complete first (job constraint), and (1,0) is on M1.\nAfter (1,0) completes at t=2, (1,1) can start on M0. M0 is free at t=0, so (1,1) starts at t=2, finishes at t=6.\nThen (0,0) starts at max(0, 6) = 6 (M0 free at 6, job ready at 0), finishes at t=9.\nJob 0\'s op 1 (on M1): job ready at t=9, M1 free at t=2 (after job 1\'s op 0), starts at t=9, finishes at t=11.\n\nMakespan = 11. Worse! Don\'t swap.\n\nSo the greedy solution is locally optimal for this example. Good.\n\nNow, what about the example\'s given solution?\n- Job 0: start[0][0]=0, start[0][1]=3\n- Job 1: start[1][0]=0, start[1][1]=5\n- Makespan = max(5, 9) = 9\n\nOur greedy gives makespan 7, which is better! So the example output is suboptimal.\n\nAlright, my algorithm is correct. Let me now write the final, complete code.\n\nI\'ll include:\n1. Greedy MWKR scheduler\n2. Local search with critical path analysis (for small/medium)\n3. Tabu search (for small)\n\nBut given time constraints, let me implement:\n1. Greedy MWKR (always)\n2. Hill climbing on machine orders (for smaller instances)\n\nHere\'s my final code structure:\n\n```cpp\n#include <bits/stdc++.h>\nusing namespace std;\n#include <chrono>\nusing namespace chrono;\n\n// Problem data\nint J, M, nOps;\nvector<vector<int>> jMach, jDur;\nvector<int> jTotWork;\nvector<int> opOff; // opOff[j] = start index for job j ops\n\ninline int opId(int j, int p) { return opOff[j] + p; }\n\n// Decode op id to (j, p)\ninline pair<int,int> decOp(int id) {\n    int j = (int)(upper_bound(opOff.begin(), opOff.end(), id) - opOff.begin()) - 1;\n    return {j, id - opOff[j]};\n}\n\n// Machine order representation\nusing MO = vector<vector<pair<int,int>>>; // mo[m] = [(j,p),...]\n\n// Evaluate schedule, return makespan (-1 if cycle)\n// Also compute EST and LST if requested\nint evalSchedule(\n    const MO& mo,\n    vector<int>* estOut = nullptr,\n    vector<int>* lstOut = nullptr,\n    vector<int>* machPredOut = nullptr,\n    vector<int>* machSuccOut = nullptr\n) {\n    vector<int> machPred(nOps, -1), machSucc(nOps, -1);\n    for(int m = 0; m < M; m++) {\n        for(int k = 1; k < (int)mo[m].size(); k++) {\n            auto [j,p] = mo[m][k];\n            auto [pj,pp] = mo[m][k-1];\n            int u = opId(j,p), v = opId(pj,pp);\n            machPred[u] = v;\n            machSucc[v] = u;\n        }\n    }\n    \n    // Build in-degrees and compute EST via Kahn\'s\n    vector<int> inDeg(nOps, 0);\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n        int sz = jMach[j].size();\n        for(int p=0;p<sz;p++) {\n            int u = opId(j,p);\n            if(p>0) inDeg[u]++;\n            if(machPred[u]>=0) inDeg[u]++;\n        }\n    }\n    \n    vector<int> est(nOps, 0);\n    vector<int> topoOrder;\n    topoOrder.reserve(nOps);\n    \n    queue<int> q;\n    for(int i=0;i<nOps;i++) if(!inDeg[i]) q.push(i);\n    \n    while(!q.empty()) {\n        int u = q.front(); q.pop();\n        topoOrder.push_back(u);\n        auto [j,p] = decOp(u);\n        int et = est[u] + jDur[j][p];\n        // job succ\n        if(p+1<(int)jMach[j].size()) {\n            int v=opId(j,p+1);\n            est[v]=max(est[v],et);\n            if(!--inDeg[v]) q.push(v);\n        }\n        // machine succ\n        if(machSucc[u]>=0) {\n            int v=machSucc[u];\n            est[v]=max(est[v],et);\n            if(!--inDeg[v]) q.push(v);\n        }\n    }\n    \n    if((int)topoOrder.size()<nOps) return -1;\n    \n    int ms=0;\n    for(int i=0;i<nOps;i++) {\n        auto [j,p]=decOp(i);\n        ms=max(ms,est[i]+jDur[j][p]);\n    }\n    \n    if(estOut) *estOut=est;\n    if(machPredOut) *machPredOut=machPred;\n    if(machSuccOut) *machSuccOut=machSucc;\n    \n    if(lstOut) {\n        // Backward pass\n        vector<int>& lft=*lstOut;\n        lft.assign(nOps,ms);\n        for(int i=(int)topoOrder.size()-1;i>=0;i--) {\n            int u=topoOrder[i];\n            auto [j,p]=decOp(u);\n            int lst_u=lft[u]-jDur[j][p];\n            if(p>0) lft[opId(j,p-1)]=min(lft[opId(j,p-1)],lst_u);\n            if(machPred[u]>=0) lft[machPred[u]]=min(lft[machPred[u]],lst_u);\n        }\n        // Convert to LST\n        for(int i=0;i<nOps;i++) {\n            auto [j,p]=decOp(i);\n            lft[i]-=jDur[j][p];\n        }\n    }\n    \n    return ms;\n}\n\n// Extract machine orders from start times\nMO extractMO(const vector<vector<int>>& start) {\n    MO mo(M);\n    for(int m=0;m<M;m++) {\n        vector<pair<int,pair<int,int>>> ops;\n        for(int j=0;j<J;j++)\n            for(int p=0;p<(int)jMach[j].size();p++)\n                if(jMach[j][p]==m)\n                    ops.push_back({start[j][p],{j,p}});\n        sort(ops.begin(),ops.end());\n        for(auto& [t,jp]:ops) mo[m].push_back(jp);\n    }\n    return mo;\n}\n\n// Greedy MWKR scheduler\nvector<vector<int>> greedyMWKR() {\n    vector<int> remWork=jTotWork;\n    vector<vector<int>> start(J);\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) start[j].resize(jMach[j].size());\n    \n    vector<int> jobNext(J,0);\n    vector<int> jobReady(J,0);\n    vector<int> machFree(M,0);\n    \n    for(int scheduled=0; scheduled<nOps; ) {\n        int t=INT_MAX;\n        for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n            if(jobNext[j]>=(int)jMach[j].size()) continue;\n            int m=jMach[j][jobNext[j]];\n            t=min(t, max(machFree[m],jobReady[j]));\n        }\n        \n        // Collect candidates\n        // Sort by remWork desc (MWKR)\n        vector<pair<int,int>> cands; // (remWork, j)\n        for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n            if(jobNext[j]>=(int)jMach[j].size()) continue;\n            int m=jMach[j][jobNext[j]];\n            if(max(machFree[m],jobReady[j])==t)\n                cands.push_back({remWork[j],j});\n        }\n        sort(cands.begin(),cands.end(),greater<>());\n        \n        vector<bool> usedM(M,false);\n        for(auto& [rw,j]:cands) {\n            int p=jobNext[j];\n            int m=jMach[j][p];\n            if(usedM[m]) continue;\n            usedM[m]=true;\n            int dur=jDur[j][p];\n            start[j][p]=t;\n            machFree[m]=t+dur;\n            jobReady[j]=t+dur;\n            remWork[j]-=dur;\n            jobNext[j]++;\n            scheduled++;\n        }\n    }\n    return start;\n}\n\n// Local search: hill climbing on machine orders\n// Tries to improve makespan by swapping consecutive ops on critical path machines\nMO localSearch(MO mo, int& bestMs, double timeLimitSec) {\n    auto t0=steady_clock::now();\n    auto elapsed=[&](){\n        return duration_cast<duration<double>>(steady_clock::now()-t0).count();\n    };\n    \n    bestMs=evalSchedule(mo);\n    MO bestMO=mo;\n    \n    bool improved=true;\n    while(improved && elapsed()<timeLimitSec) {\n        improved=false;\n        \n        // Get current EST and LST for critical path\n        vector<int> est,lst;\n        int ms=evalSchedule(mo,&est,&lst);\n        \n        // Find critical path ops: EST[u] == LST[u]\n        // Find critical machine arcs\n        \n        int bestGain=0;\n        int bestM=-1, bestK=-1;\n        \n        for(int m=0;m<M;m++) {\n            for(int k=0;k+1<(int)mo[m].size();k++) {\n                if(elapsed()>=timeLimitSec) goto done;\n                \n                auto [j1,p1]=mo[m][k];\n                auto [j2,p2]=mo[m][k+1];\n                int u=opId(j1,p1), v=opId(j2,p2);\n                \n                // Both must be on critical path\n                if(est[u]!=lst[u] || est[v]!=lst[v]) continue;\n                \n                // Try swap\n                swap(mo[m][k],mo[m][k+1]);\n                int newMs=evalSchedule(mo);\n                if(newMs>0 && newMs<ms) {\n                    int gain=ms-newMs;\n                    if(gain>bestGain) {\n                        bestGain=gain;\n                        bestM=m; bestK=k;\n                    }\n                }\n                // Revert\n                swap(mo[m][k],mo[m][k+1]);\n            }\n        }\n        \n        if(bestGain>0) {\n            swap(mo[bestM][bestK],mo[bestM][bestK+1]);\n            ms-=bestGain;\n            if(ms<bestMs) {\n                bestMs=ms;\n                bestMO=mo;\n            }\n            improved=true;\n        }\n    }\n    done:\n    return bestMO;\n}\n\nint main() {\n    ios::sync_with_stdio(false);\n    cin.tie(nullptr);\n    \n    cin>>J>>M;\n    jMach.resize(J); jDur.resize(J); The key issue is that only swapping consecutive ops on the critical path is guaranteed to be a useful move. Other swaps either:\n- Don\'t affect the makespan (if neither op is on CP)\n- Could increase or decrease makespan (if only one is on CP)\n\nFor a more robust search, let me also try non-critical swaps sometimes (e.g., in a tabu search framework).\n\nBut for simplicity, let me just do:\n1. Try all consecutive pairs on all machines\n2. If swap improves, keep it\n3. Repeat until time limit or no improvement\n\nThis is O(num_pairs * evaluation_cost) per pass = O(nOps * nOps) per pass.\nFor nOps=500: O(250k) per pass, many passes in 5 seconds.\nFor nOps=2000: O(4M) per pass, limited passes.\nFor nOps=10000: O(100M) per pass, maybe 1-2 passes.\nFor nOps=50000: too slow, skip.\n\nSo:\n- nOps <= 500: full hill climbing\n- nOps <= 5000: critical path only\n- nOps > 5000: just greedy\n\nLet me set the threshold based on a time estimate.\n\nActually, I realize I should also try multiple restarts with different random orderings of the greedy to escape local optima. But let\'s keep it simple.\n\nOne more thing: for VERY large instances, the greedy scheduler itself might be slow (O(nOps * J)). For J=10000, nOps=10000: O(100M). Should be OK.\n\nBut using a set for usedM is O(M log M) per scheduled op. For M=50: negligible. I\'ll use a simple boolean array instead.\n\nAlright, let me now write the complete, final C++ code:\n\n```cpp\n#include <bits/stdc++.h>\nusing namespace std;\nusing ll = long long;\nusing namespace chrono;\n\nstatic int J, M, nOps;\nstatic vector<vector<int>> jMach, jDur;\nstatic vector<int> jTotWork;\nstatic vector<int> opOff;\n\nstatic inline int opId(int j, int p) { return opOff[j] + p; }\n\nstatic inline pair<int,int> decOp(int id) {\n    // Binary search for j\n    int lo=0, hi=J-1;\n    while(lo<hi) {\n        int mid=(lo+hi+1)/2;\n        if(opOff[mid]<=id) lo=mid; else hi=mid-1;\n    }\n    return {lo, id-opOff[lo]};\n}\n\nusing MO = vector<vector<pair<int,int>>>;\n\nstatic int evalSchedule(\n    const MO& mo,\n    vector<int>* estOut=nullptr,\n    vector<int>* lstOut=nullptr\n) {\n    vector<int> machSucc(nOps,-1), machPred(nOps,-1);\n    for(int m=0;m<M;m++) {\n        for(int k=1;k<(int)mo[m].size();k++) {\n            auto [j,p]=mo[m][k];\n            auto [pj,pp]=mo[m][k-1];\n            int u=opId(j,p), v=opId(pj,pp);\n            machPred[u]=v;\n            machSucc[v]=u;\n        }\n    }\n    \n    vector<int> inDeg(nOps,0);\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n        int sz=(int)jMach[j].size();\n        for(int p=0;p<sz;p++) {\n            if(p>0) inDeg[opId(j,p)]++;\n            if(machPred[opId(j,p)]>=0) inDeg[opId(j,p)]++;\n        }\n    }\n    \n    vector<int> est(nOps,0);\n    vector<int> topo;\n    topo.reserve(nOps);\n    \n    // Use vector as queue for speed\n    vector<int> bfsQ;\n    bfsQ.reserve(nOps);\n    for(int i=0;i<nOps;i++) if(!inDeg[i]) bfsQ.push_back(i);\n    \n    int head=0;\n    while(head<(int)bfsQ.size()) {\n        int u=bfsQ[head++];\n        topo.push_back(u);\n        auto [j,p]=decOp(u);\n        int et=est[u]+jDur[j][p];\n        if(p+1<(int)jMach[j].size()) {\n            int v=opId(j,p+1);\n            est[v]=max(est[v],et);\n            if(!--inDeg[v]) bfsQ.push_back(v);\n        }\n        if(machSucc[u]>=0) {\n            int v=machSucc[u];\n            est[v]=max(est[v],et);\n            if(!--inDeg[v]) bfsQ.push_back(v);\n        }\n    }\n    \n    if((int)topo.size()<nOps) return -1; // cycle\n    \n    int ms=0;\n    for(int i=0;i<nOps;i++) {\n        auto [j,p]=decOp(i);\n        ms=max(ms,est[i]+jDur[j][p]);\n    }\n    \n    if(estOut) *estOut=est;\n    \n    if(lstOut) {\n        vector<int>& lft=*lstOut;\n        lft.assign(nOps,ms);\n        for(int i=(int)topo.size()-1;i>=0;i--) {\n            int u=topo[i];\n            auto [j,p]=decOp(u);\n            int lstU=lft[u]-jDur[j][p];\n            if(p>0) { int v=opId(j,p-1); lft[v]=min(lft[v],lstU); }\n            if(machPred[u]>=0) { int v=machPred[u]; lft[v]=min(lft[v],lstU); }\n        }\n        for(int i=0;i<nOps;i++) { auto [j,p]=decOp(i); lft[i]-=jDur[j][p]; }\n    }\n    \n    return ms;\n}\n\nstatic MO extractMO(const vector<vector<int>>& start) {\n    MO mo(M);\n    // For each machine, collect all ops and sort by start time\n    vector<vector<pair<int,pair<int,int>>>> machOps(M);\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++)\n        for(int p=0;p<(int)jMach[j].size();p++)\n            machOps[jMach[j][p]].push_back({start[j][p],{j,p}});\n    for(int m=0;m<M;m++) {\n        sort(machOps[m].begin(),machOps[m].end());\n        for(auto& [t,jp]:machOps[m]) mo[m].push_back(jp);\n    }\n    return mo;\n}\n\nstatic vector<vector<int>> greedyMWKR() {\n    vector<int> remWork=jTotWork;\n    vector<vector<int>> start(J);\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) start[j].resize(jMach[j].size());\n    \n    vector<int> jobNext(J,0);\n    vector<int> jobReady(J,0);\n    vector<int> machFree(M,0);\n    vector<bool> usedM(M,false);\n    \n    for(int scheduled=0; scheduled<nOps; ) {\n        // Find minimum time\n        int t=INT_MAX;\n        for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n            if(jobNext[j]>=(int)jMach[j].size()) continue;\n            int m=jMach[j][jobNext[j]];\n            int st=max(machFree[m],jobReady[j]);\n            if(st<t) t=st;\n        }\n        \n        // Collect candidates at time t\n        // Sort by remWork descending\n        static vector<pair<int,int>> cands;\n        cands.clear();\n        for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n            if(jobNext[j]>=(int)jMach[j].size()) continue;\n            int m=jMach[j][jobNext[j]];\n            if(max(machFree[m],jobReady[j])==t)\n                cands.push_back({remWork[j],j});\n        }\n        sort(cands.begin(),cands.end(),greater<pair<int,int>>());\n        \n        fill(usedM.begin(),usedM.end(),false);\n        for(auto& [rw,j]:cands) {\n            int p=jobNext[j];\n            int m=jMach[j][p];\n            if(usedM[m]) continue;\n            usedM[m]=true;\n            int dur=jDur[j][p];\n            start[j][p]=t;\n            machFree[m]=t+dur;\n            jobReady[j]=t+dur;\n            remWork[j]-=dur;\n            jobNext[j]++;\n            scheduled++;\n        }\n    }\n    return start;\n}\n\n// Same as greedyMWKR but uses SPT (shortest processing time) priority\nstatic vector<vector<int>> greedySPT() {\n    vector<vector<int>> start(J);\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) start[j].resize(jMach[j].size());\n    \n    vector<int> jobNext(J,0);\n    vector<int> jobReady(J,0);\n    vector<int> machFree(M,0);\n    vector<bool> usedM(M,false);\n    \n    for(int scheduled=0; scheduled<nOps; ) {\n        int t=INT_MAX;\n        for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n            if(jobNext[j]>=(int)jMach[j].size()) continue;\n            int m=jMach[j][jobNext[j]];\n            int st=max(machFree[m],jobReady[j]);\n            if(st<t) t=st;\n        }\n        \n        static vector<pair<int,int>> cands;\n        cands.clear();\n        for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n            if(jobNext[j]>=(int)jMach[j].size()) continue;\n            int m=jMach[j][jobNext[j]];\n            if(max(machFree[m],jobReady[j])==t)\n                cands.push_back({jDur[j][jobNext[j]],j}); // SPT: shorter is better\n        }\n        sort(cands.begin(),cands.end()); // ascending (SPT)\n        \n        fill(usedM.begin(),usedM.end(),false);\n        for(auto& [rw,j]:cands) {\n            int p=jobNext[j];\n            int m=jMach[j][p];\n            if(usedM[m]) continue;\n            usedM[m]=true;\n            int dur=jDur[j][p];\n            start[j][p]=t;\n            machFree[m]=t+dur;\n            jobReady[j]=t+dur;\n            jobNext[j]++;\n            scheduled++;\n        }\n    }\n    return start;\n}\n\n// Local search: try swapping all consecutive pairs on all machines\n// Returns best makespan and updates mo and estOut\nstatic int doLocalSearch(MO& mo, vector<int>& bestEst, double timeLimitSec, bool cpOnly) {\n    auto t0=steady_clock::now();\n    auto elapsed=[&](){\n        return duration_cast<duration<double>>(steady_clock::now()-t0).count();\n    };\n    \n    vector<int> est, lst;\n    int ms=evalSchedule(mo, &est, cpOnly?&lst:nullptr);\n    bestEst=est;\n    \n    bool improved=true;\n    while(improved && elapsed()<timeLimitSec) {\n        improved=false;\n        \n        if(cpOnly) {\n            // Recompute critical path info\n            ms=evalSchedule(mo, &est, &lst);\n        }\n        \n        for(int m=0;m<M && elapsed()<timeLimitSec;m++) {\n            for(int k=0;k+1<(int)mo[m].size() && elapsed()<timeLimitSec;k++) {\n                auto [j1,p1]=mo[m][k];\n                auto [j2,p2]=mo[m][k+1];\n                int u=opId(j1,p1), v=opId(j2,p2);\n                \n                if(cpOnly && (est[u]!=lst[u] || est[v]!=lst[v])) continue;\n                \n                swap(mo[m][k],mo[m][k+1]);\n                int newMs=evalSchedule(mo);\n                if(newMs>0 && newMs<ms) {\n                    ms=newMs;\n                    evalSchedule(mo,&est,cpOnly?&lst:nullptr);\n                    bestEst=est;\n                    improved=true;\n                    break; // restart machine loop\n                }\n                swap(mo[m][k],mo[m][k+1]); // revert\n            }\n            if(improved) break;\n        }\n    }\n    return ms;\n}\n\nint main() {\n    ios::sync_with_stdio(false);\n    cin.tie(nullptr);\n    \n    cin>>J>>M;\n    jMach.resize(J); jDur.resize(J); jTotWork.resize(J,0);\n    opOff.resize(J+1,0);\n    \n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n        int T; cin>>T;\n        jMach[j].resize(T); jDur[j].resize(T);\n        for(int p=0;p<T;p++) {\n            cin>>jMach[j][p]>>jDur[j][p];\n            jTotWork[j]+=jDur[j][p];\n        }\n        opOff[j+1]=opOff[j]+T;\n    }\n    nOps=opOff[J];\n    \n    // Multiple greedy solutions\n    auto start1=greedyMWKR();\n    auto start2=greedySPT();\n    \n    // Pick better one by evaluating\n    auto mo1=extractMO(start1);\n    auto mo2=extractMO(start2);\n    int ms1=evalSchedule(mo1);\n    int ms2=evalSchedule(mo2);\n    \n    MO bestMO;\n    vector<vector<int>> bestStart;\n    int bestMs;\n    \n    if(ms1<=ms2) { bestMO=mo1; bestStart=start1; bestMs=ms1; }\n    else { bestMO=mo2; bestStart=start2; bestMs=ms2; }\n    \n    // Local search\n    auto tStart=steady_clock::now();\n    double totalTimeLimitSec=5.0; // 5 second total time limit\n    \n    if(nOps<=50000) { // only for manageable sizes\n        double timeForLS=totalTimeLimitSec - \n            duration_cast<duration<double>>(steady_clock::now()-tStart).count();\n        timeForLS=max(0.0,timeForLS-0.1); // leave 0.1s for output\n        \n        bool cpOnly=(nOps>1000);\n        \n        vector<int> newEst;\n        int newMs=doLocalSearch(bestMO, newEst, timeForLS, cpOnly);\n        if(newMs<bestMs) {\n            bestMs=newMs;\n            // Update bestStart from newEst\n            bestStart.resize(J);\n            for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n                bestStart[j].resize(jMach[j].size());\n                for(int p=0;p<(int)jMach[j].size();p++)\n                    bestStart[j][p]=newEst[opId(j,p)];\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    // Output\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n        for(int p=0;p<(int)jMach[j].size();p++) {\n            if(p>0) cout<<\' \';\n            cout<<bestStart[j][p]<<\' \'<<jMach[j][p];\n        }\n        cout<<\'\\n\';\n    }\n    \n    return 0;\n}\n```\n\nWait, I have a problem with `static vector<pair<int,int>> cands` inside a function - this is a C extension and not safe in recursive contexts, but since the greedy functions are not recursive, it\'s fine but could be problematic if called from multiple threads. Since we\'re single-threaded here, it\'s OK.\n\nActually, better to just use a local vector to avoid any issues.\n\nAlso, I realize my `doLocalSearch` is doing first-improvement (breaks on first improvement per pass). For better quality, I should try all pairs and take best improvement. But this is tricky because after one swap, the critical path changes.\n\nLet me use a simpler strategy: in each pass, scan all pairs and take the first improving swap, then restart. This is the first-improvement hill climbing.\n\nFor time efficiency, I\'ll break out of the inner loop as soon as I find an improvement.\n\nLet me also think about whether my `evalSchedule` is correct. The issue is that when I build the successor list, I need to handle potential duplicate edges (if machSucc[u] == opId(j,p+1) for some job and machine relation).\n\nActually in JSSP, a job\'s consecutive ops are on different machines (otherwise we\'d just have a longer op on the same machine). So there\'s no duplicate edge issue.\n\nWait, actually, I\'m not sure about this. The problem says "Each task in a job must run on its specified machine" and tasks within a job must execute in order. Two consecutive tasks can be on the same machine - the problem doesn\'t say they can\'t. But in practice, it would be unusual.\n\nIf two consecutive tasks of the same job are on the same machine, they should still be serialized (first one, then the second). In my machine order, they would appear consecutively on that machine for that job. This is handled correctly.\n\nHmm, but there could be a subtle issue: if tasks (j,p) and (j,p+1) are both on machine m, and they appear consecutively in machOrder[m] (which they must since they must be in this order), then:\n- inDeg[opId(j,p+1)] gets incremented for: job pred (j,p) and machine pred (j,p)\n- Both are the same op! This would double-count.\n\nLet me handle this case: if job predecessor is the same as machine predecessor, don\'t double-count.\n\nBut actually, in my current code:\n```cpp\nif(p>0) inDeg[opId(j,p)]++; // job pred\nif(machPred[opId(j,p)]>=0) inDeg[opId(j,p)]++; // machine pred\n```\n\nIf (j,p-1) and (j,p) are on the same machine AND (j,p-1) is immediately before (j,p) in machOrder, then machPred[opId(j,p)] = opId(j,p-1). So inDeg would be incremented twice for the same dependency.\n\nIn the forward pass, I add:\n- edge from opId(j,p-1) to opId(j,p) for job order\n- edge from opId(j,p-1) to opId(j,p) for machine order (same edge!)\n\nThe BFS would then try to decrement inDeg[opId(j,p)] twice, but it would reach 0 after the first decrement (if the initial inDeg is 2) - that\'s wrong. The node would be processed when inDeg reaches 1, not 0, and then decrement to 0 without re-adding.\n\nWait, inDeg=2 means two decrement needed. The first successor processing decrements to 1, the second processing decrements to 0 and adds to queue. But both processings are from the SAME predecessor. Let me trace:\n\n- opId(j,p-1) is processed, et = start + dur\n- Update job succ opId(j,p): est[v] = max(est[v], et), inDeg[v]--; → if inDeg[v]==0, enqueue\n- Update mach succ opId(j,p): est[v] = max(est[v], et), inDeg[v]--; → if inDeg[v]==0, enqueue\n\nSo if inDeg was 2, after first decrement it\'s 1 (not enqueued), after second decrement it\'s 0 (enqueued). But we\'ve updated est[v] twice with the same value. That\'s actually fine! The EST is set correctly.\n\nBut wait, I\'m adding two edges from u to v:\n- succ[opId(j,p-1)].push_back(opId(j,p)) // from job order\n- succ[opId(j,p-1)].push_back(opId(j,p)) // from machine order (same!)\n\nSo when processing opId(j,p-1), I try to update opId(j,p) twice. The second time, inDeg might already be 0 and the node already in queue. Then we\'d process it again → incorrect behavior!\n\nTo fix: deduplicate edges, or don\'t add machine edge if it\'s the same as job edge.\n\nFix:\n```cpp\nif(p>0) inDeg[opId(j,p)]++;\nif(machPred[opId(j,p)]>=0 && machPred[opId(j,p)]!=opId(j,p-1))\n    inDeg[opId(j,p)]++;\n```\n\nAnd for succ:\n```cpp\n// job succ\nif(p+1<(int)jMach[j].size()) {\n    int v=opId(j,p+1);\n    est[v]=max(est[v],et);\n    if(!--inDeg[v]) bfsQ.push_back(v);\n}\n// machine succ (only if different from job succ)\nif(machSucc[u]>=0) {\n    int v=machSucc[u];\n    if(p+1>=(int)jMach[j].size() || v!=opId(j,p+1)) {\n        est[v]=max(est[v],et);\n        if(!--inDeg[v]) bfsQ.push_back(v);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis is getting complicated. Let me think of a cleaner way.\n\nActually, the simplest fix: just don\'t add machine edges for ops that are consecutive in the same job AND consecutive in the same machine AND same predecessor. We can detect this by checking if the machine predecessor equals the job predecessor.\n\nOr even simpler: since the job constraint subsumes the machine constraint when they have the same predecessor, we can just skip the machine edge if it\'s redundant:\n\nIn the `evalSchedule` function, when building edges:\n```cpp\nfor(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n    for(int p=0;p<sz;p++) {\n        int u=opId(j,p);\n        // Job order edge\n        if(p>0) {\n            succ[opId(j,p-1)].push_back(u);\n            inDeg[u]++;\n        }\n        // Machine order edge (only if not same as job order)\n        int mp=machPred[u];\n        if(mp>=0) {\n            // Don\'t add if mp is job predecessor (already added above)\n            if(p>0 && mp==opId(j,p-1)) {} // skip redundant\n            else {\n                succ[mp].push_back(u);\n                inDeg[u]++;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis is correct! If machPred[u] == jobPred[u], the machine edge is redundant (job edge already handles the constraint), so we skip it.\n\nBut actually, even if redundant, having it doesn\'t cause CORRECTNESS issues as long as we handle inDeg properly. The issue I pointed out earlier about "double processing" is real though.\n\nLet me trace again with deduplication:\n- opId(j,p-1) to opId(j,p): ONLY job edge (machine edge skipped)\n- succ[opId(j,p-1)] = [opId(j,p)] (one entry)\n- inDeg[opId(j,p)] = 1 (from job pred only)\n- When processing opId(j,p-1): update opId(j,p) once, inDeg→0, enqueue. ✓\n\nGreat, this is correct.\n\nBut wait, what about the BACKWARD pass? I need to handle this symmetrically. In the backward pass:\n```cpp\nint lstU=lft[u]-jDur[j][p];\nif(p>0) { int v=opId(j,p-1); lft[v]=min(lft[v],lstU); }\n// machine pred\nif(machPred[u]>=0) {\n    int v=machPred[u];\n    if(p==0 || v!=opId(j,p-1)) // skip if same as job pred\n        lft[v]=min(lft[v],lstU);\n}\n```\n\nOK let me restructure the code more carefully to handle edge deduplication properly.\n\nActually, you know what - let me just collect all edges explicitly (as a set to avoid duplicates) and then build the graph:\n\n```cpp\nset<pair<int,int>> edges;\nfor(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n    for(int p=1;p<(int)jMach[j].size();p++)\n        edges.insert({opId(j,p-1), opId(j,p)});\n}\nfor(int m=0;m<M;m++) {\n    for(int k=1;k<(int)mo[m].size();k++) {\n        auto [j,p]=mo[m][k];\n        auto [pj,pp]=mo[m][k-1];\n        edges.insert({opId(pj,pp), opId(j,p)});\n    }\n}\n// Build adj list from edges\nfor(auto [u,v]:edges) {\n    succ[u].push_back(v);\n    inDeg[v]++;\n}\n```\n\nThis uses a set to deduplicate edges. For nOps=50k, edges ≤ 100k, using a set is O(n log n) which is fine.\n\nBut this adds significant overhead. Let me use a faster deduplication:\n\n```cpp\nfor(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n    for(int p=1;p<(int)jMach[j].size();p++) {\n        succ[opId(j,p-1)].push_back(opId(j,p));\n        inDeg[opId(j,p)]++;\n    }\n}\nfor(int m=0;m<M;m++) {\n    for(int k=1;k<(int)mo[m].size();k++) {\n        auto [j,p]=mo[m][k];\n        auto [pj,pp]=mo[m][k-1];\n        int u=opId(pj,pp), v=opId(j,p);\n        // Check if this edge is already added (as job order)\n        bool alreadyAdded=(p>0 && u==opId(j,p-1));\n        if(!alreadyAdded) {\n            succ[u].push_back(v);\n            inDeg[v]++;\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThis is O(nOps + edges) without set overhead.\n\nThe check `p>0 && u==opId(j,p-1)` checks if the machine predecessor is the same as the job predecessor.\n\nBut wait: machPred of (j,p) could be job predecessor AND machine predecessor simultaneously only if two consecutive ops of the same job are on the same machine AND are consecutive on that machine. Let\'s check:\n- If jMach[j][p-1] == jMach[j][p] (same machine), and in machOrder[m], (j,p-1) comes immediately before (j,p).\n\nIn this case, the machine edge is (j,p-1) → (j,p), which is the same as the job edge. So we skip it.\n\nBut what if jMach[j][p-1] == jMach[j][p] but another job\'s op comes between them in machOrder[m]? Then the machine predecessor of (j,p) would be some other op, not (j,p-1). In this case, the machine edge is not redundant.\n\nMy check `p>0 && u==opId(j,p-1)` handles this correctly: u is the machine predecessor, and we check if it equals the job predecessor.\n\nOK great. Let me now think about backward pass deduplication. In the backward pass, I update predecessors. I process each node u and update its predecessors.\n\nFor each node u, its predecessors are:\n1. Job predecessor: opId(j, p-1) if p>0\n2. Machine predecessor: machPred[u] if not same as job pred\n\nIn the backward pass:\n```cpp\nfor(int i=(int)topo.size()-1;i>=0;i--) {\n    int u=topo[i];\n    auto [j,p]=decOp(u);\n    int lstU=lft[u]-jDur[j][p];\n    // Update job predecessor\n    if(p>0) {\n        int v=opId(j,p-1);\n        lft[v]=min(lft[v],lstU);\n    }\n    // Update machine predecessor (if not same as job pred)\n    if(machPred[u]>=0) {\n        int v=machPred[u];\n        bool sameAsJobPred=(p>0 && v==opId(j,p-1));\n        if(!sameAsJobPred)\n            lft[v]=min(lft[v],lstU);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nBut wait - the backward pass should update lft[v] for each EDGE (v, u). If there\'s only ONE edge from v to u (because we deduplicated), then we only update once. That\'s correct!\n\nIf v is both job pred and machine pred (same node), and we update lft[v] = min(lft[v], lstU) only once - that\'s fine because the update is the same either way.\n\nActually, even if we update twice with the same value, it doesn\'t matter (min is idempotent). The issue was only with the BFS in-degree counter for forward pass. For backward pass, there\'s no in-degree counter - we just propagate min values. So duplicating the backward update is harmless (just redundant work).\n\nSo the backward pass can be written without deduplication concern:\n\n```cpp\n// Backward pass\nvector<int>& lft=*lstOut;\nlft.assign(nOps,ms);\nfor(int i=(int)topo.size()-1;i>=0;i--) {\n    int u=topo[i];\n    auto [j,p]=decOp(u);\n    int lstU=lft[u]-jDur[j][p];\n    if(p>0) lft[opId(j,p-1)]=min(lft[opId(j,p-1)],lstU);\n    if(machPred[u]>=0) lft[machPred[u]]=min(lft[machPred[u]],lstU);\n}\n// Convert to LST\nfor(int i=0;i<nOps;i++) { auto [j,p]=decOp(i); lft[i]-=jDur[j][p]; }\n```\n\nEven if we update lft[v] twice when v is both job pred and machine pred, it doesn\'t matter since min(lft[v], lstU) twice gives the same result as once.\n\nBut wait, in this case for the forward pass, if we had a duplicate edge (u→v twice), the in-degree would be 2 and we\'d need two triggers from u. But u can only process v twice if it\'s in succ[u] twice. If I correctly avoid adding the duplicate in succ, then inDeg is 1 and succ has one entry. 👍\n\nOK let me also handle the case where the machPred check in forward pass is wrong. The machine predecessor is `machPred[u]` which I compute from the machine order. The job predecessor is `opId(j, p-1)`. The check `p>0 && machPred[u]==opId(j,p-1)` correctly identifies if they\'re the same.\n\nActually, I realize there\'s another issue with my `evalSchedule` function. I\'m building `machPred` and `machSucc` for each op, but I\'m also building `succ` and `inDeg` in the same function. The `succ` from machine order might add edges that are also in the job order. Let me make this clear:\n\nHere\'s the corrected evalSchedule:\n\n```cpp\nstatic int evalSchedule(\n    const MO& mo,\n    vector<int>* estOut=nullptr,\n    vector<int>* lstOut=nullptr,\n    vector<int>* machPredIdOut=nullptr\n) {\n    // Build machPred\n    vector<int> machPred(nOps, -1);\n    for(int m=0;m<M;m++) {\n        for(int k=1;k<(int)mo[m].size();k++) {\n            auto [j,p]=mo[m][k];\n            auto [pj,pp]=mo[m][k-1];\n            machPred[opId(j,p)]=opId(pj,pp);\n        }\n    }\n    \n    if(machPredIdOut) *machPredIdOut=machPred;\n    \n    // Build graph (deduplicated)\n    vector<int> inDeg(nOps,0);\n    vector<vector<int>> succ(nOps);\n    \n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n        for(int p=0;p<(int)jMach[j].size();p++) {\n            int u=opId(j,p);\n            // Job order edge\n            if(p>0) {\n                int v=opId(j,p-1);\n                succ[v].push_back(u);\n                inDeg[u]++;\n            }\n            // Machine order edge (skip if same as job order)\n            if(machPred[u]>=0) {\n                int v=machPred[u];\n                bool dup=(p>0 && v==opId(j,p-1));\n                if(!dup) {\n                    succ[v].push_back(u);\n                    inDeg[u]++;\n                }\n            }\n        }\n    }\n    \n    // Forward pass (Kahn\'s)\n    vector<int> est(nOps,0);\n    vector<int> topo;\n    topo.reserve(nOps);\n    \n    vector<int> bfsQ;\n    bfsQ.reserve(nOps);\n    for(int i=0;i<nOps;i++) if(!inDeg[i]) bfsQ.push_back(i);\n    \n    int head=0;\n    while(head<(int)bfsQ.size()) {\n        int u=bfsQ[head++];\n        topo.push_back(u);\n        auto [j,p]=decOp(u);\n        int et=est[u]+jDur[j][p];\n        for(int v:succ[u]) {\n            est[v]=max(est[v],et);\n            if(!--inDeg[v]) bfsQ.push_back(v);\n        }\n    }\n    \n    if((int)topo.size()<nOps) return -1; // cycle\n    \n    int ms=0;\n    for(int i=0;i<nOps;i++) {\n        auto [j,p]=decOp(i);\n        ms=max(ms,est[i]+jDur[j][p]);\n    }\n    \n    if(estOut) *estOut=est;\n    \n    if(lstOut) {\n        vector<int>& lft=*lstOut;\n        lft.assign(nOps,ms);\n        for(int i=(int)topo.size()-1;i>=0;i--) {\n            int u=topo[i];\n            auto [j,p]=decOp(u);\n            int lstU=lft[u]-jDur[j][p];\n            if(p>0) lft[opId(j,p-1)]=min(lft[opId(j,p-1)],lstU);\n            if(machPred[u]>=0) lft[machPred[u]]=min(lft[machPred[u]],lstU);\n        }\n        for(int i=0;i<nOps;i++) { auto [j,p]=decOp(i); lft[i]-=jDur[j][p]; }\n    }\n    \n    return ms;\n}\n```\n\nThis looks correct to me. The decOp function uses binary search to decode op IDs. For frequently called functions, this might be slow. Let me precompute a decode table:\n\n```cpp\nstatic vector<int> opJ, opP; // opJ[id] = job, opP[id] = position within job\n// Precompute once\nvoid precomputeDecode() {\n    opJ.resize(nOps);\n    opP.resize(nOps);\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++)\n        for(int p=0;p<(int)jMach[j].size();p++) {\n            opJ[opId(j,p)]=j;\n            opP[opId(j,p)]=p;\n        }\n}\n```\n\nThis allows O(1) decode instead of O(log J). For large instances, this is a significant speedup.\n\nLet me include this optimization.\n\nNow let me also think about the tabu search. For medium instances, simple hill climbing might not escape local optima. Tabu search maintains a "tabu list" of recently visited solutions and allows non-improving moves.\n\nFor simplicity, I\'ll use:\n- Tabu list: set of (m, k) pairs (machine, position) that have been recently swapped\n- Tabu tenure: 7 (number of iterations a swap stays in tabu list)\n- Accept: best non-tabu move, even if non-improving (unless makespan is worse than best)\n- Aspiration: if a tabu move leads to a new best, accept it anyway\n\nThis is the basic tabu search for JSSP.\n\nFor the neighborhood: try ALL consecutive pairs on ALL machines (N1 neighborhood).\n\nFor each iteration:\n1. Compute all possible swaps (N1 neighborhood)\n2. Evaluate each swap\n3. Find best non-tabu swap (or tabu but aspiration)\n4. Apply it\n5. Add to tabu list\n\nThis requires evaluating |N1| = O(nOps) swaps per iteration, each costing O(nOps), so O(nOps²) per iteration. For nOps=500: O(250k) per iteration, feasible.\n\nFor nOps=5000: O(25M) per iteration, too slow for many iterations. So for larger instances, use CP-only (critical path) neighborhood.\n\nOK let me put together the final code now. I\'ll be more systematic.\n\nActually, I think I need to step back and write this more carefully. Let me outline what I want:\n\n1. Fast MWKR greedy\n2. Fast SPT greedy  \n3. Efficient evalSchedule (O(nOps) using precomputed decode tables)\n4. Critical path computation\n5. Tabu search on critical path neighborhood (for small/medium)\n6. Adaptive time management\n\nHere\'s a cleaner code structure:\n\n```cpp\n#include <bits/stdc++.h>\nusing namespace std;\nusing namespace chrono;\n\n// Global problem data\nint J, M, Let me check:\n- `bfsQ` is initialized with nodes having inDeg=0\n- During processing, nodes are added when their inDeg reaches 0\n- If there\'s a cycle, some nodes will never have inDeg=0 and won\'t be added\n- Final size of bfsQ = number of processed nodes ≤ nOps ✓\n\nAlright, the code is correct. Let me now think about allocating these vectors. For performance, I should avoid allocating large vectors in every call to `evalFast` (which is called many times in the search).\n\nFor a tabu search with many iterations, allocating and deallocating vectors of size nOps each iteration is expensive.\n\nSolution: preallocate these vectors as global/static variables and reuse them.\n\nBut then the function is not reentrant. Since we\'re single-threaded, this is fine.\n\nLet me preallocate:\n\n```cpp\n// Preallocated working space\nstatic vector<int> _machPred, _jobSucc, _machSucc, _inDeg, _est, _bfsQ, _topo, _lft;\n\nvoid allocWorkspace() {\n    _machPred.resize(nOps);\n    _jobSucc.resize(nOps);\n    _machSucc.resize(nOps);\n    _inDeg.resize(nOps);\n    _est.resize(nOps);\n    _bfsQ.resize(nOps);\n    _topo.resize(nOps);\n    _lft.resize(nOps);\n}\n```\n\nThen in eval functions, use these preallocated vectors.\n\nThis avoids repeated allocation. The fill/assign operations are still O(nOps) but memset-like operations are fast.\n\nActually, for nOps=50k, these vectors are ~50k*4 bytes = 200KB each. 8 vectors = 1.6MB. Well within memory limits.\n\nBut using global/static vectors requires resetting them each call. `fill` or `assign` is O(n). So total overhead is still O(n) per eval call.\n\nFor 10000 tabu iterations on a 50k-op instance: 10000 * O(50k) = 500M ops. Might be borderline.\n\nActually, for large instances I\'ll just skip the local search. So for the local search cases (nOps <= 5000), the overhead is manageable.\n\nLet me now think about the tabu search implementation. The standard tabu search for JSSP:\n\n**Tabu search parameters:**\n- Tabu list: set of recently applied moves (swaps)\n- Tabu tenure: 5-15 iterations a move is forbidden\n- Max iterations: function of problem size and time\n\n**Move representation:**\n- Move = swap of two consecutive ops (m, k, k+1) on machine m\n- After applying, the reverse move (m, k, k+1) is tabu for tenure iterations\n\n**Neighborhood:**\n- N1: all consecutive pairs on all machines (all swaps)\n- Critical path only: only pairs where both ops are on CP\n\n**Selection:**\n- Find best non-tabu move (minimize makespan)\n- If best tabu move leads to new global best, apply (aspiration)\n\nFor my implementation, I\'ll use critical-path-only neighborhood since it\'s smaller and usually more effective.\n\nAlright, let me now write the complete code. I\'ll be concise but correct:\n\nLet me write the full code now without further deliberation:\n\n```cpp\n#include <bits/stdc++.h>\nusing namespace std;\nusing namespace chrono;\n\nstatic int J, M, nOps;\nstatic vector<vector<int>> jMach, jDur;\nstatic vector<int> jTotWork;\nstatic vector<int> opOff, opJ_, opP_;\n\nvoid setup() {\n    opOff.resize(J+1); opOff[0]=0;\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++)       int u=oid(j,p),v=oid(pj,pp);\n            g_machPred[u]=v;\n            g_machSucc[v]=u;\n        }\n    }\n    \n    // jobSucc\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n        int priority) {\n    // priority: 0=MWKR, 1=SPT\n    vector<vector<int>> start(J);\n    for(int j=0;j<J;j++) start[j].resize(jMach[j].size());\n    \n    vector<int> remWork=jTotWork;\n    vector<int> j=0;j<J;j++) {\n            if(jobNext[j]>=(int)jMach[j].size()) continue;\n            int m=jMach[j][jobNext[j]];\n            int st=max(machFree[m],jobReady[j]);\n            if(st<t) t=st;\n        }\n        \n        // Collect candidates\n        struct Cand { int key,j; };\n        static vector<Cand> cands;\n        cands.clear();\n        for(int j=0;j<J;j++) {\n            if(jobNext[j]>=(int)jMach[j].size()) continue;\n            int m=jMach[j][jobNext[j]];\n            if(max(machFree[m],jobReady[j])!=t) continue;\n            int key=(priority==0) ? -remWork[j] : jDur[j][jobNext[j]];\n            cands.push_back({key,j});\n        }\n        sort(cands.begin(),cands.end(),[](const Cand&a,const Cand&b){return a.key<b.key;});\n        \n        fill(usedM.begin(),usedM.end(),false);\n        for(auto& [key,j]:cands) {\n            int p=jobNext[j];\n            int m=jMach[j][p];\n            if(usedM[m]) continue;\n            usedM[m]=true;\n            int dur=jDur[j][p];\n            start[j][p]=t;\n            machFree[m]=t+dur;\n            jobReady[j]=t+dur;\n            remWork[j]-=dur;\n            jobNext[j]++;\n Let me double check the MWKR and SPT keys:\n   - MWKR: schedule job with MOST remaining work first → sort by remWork DESC → key=-remWork, sort ascending (smallest key = largest remWork)\n   - SPT: schedule job with SHORTEST next task first → sort by duration ASC → key=duration, sort ascending\n\n   In my code:\n   ```cpp\n   int key=(priority==0) ? -remWork[j] : jDur[j][jobNext[j]];\n   cands.push_back({key,j});\n   sort(cands.begin(),cands.end(),[](const Cand&a,const Cand&b){return a.key<b.key;});\n   ```\n   \n   MWKR: key=-remWork, sort ascending → smaller key = larger remWork → MWKR correct ✓\n   SPT: key=duration, sort ascending → smaller key = shorter duration → SPT correct ✓\n\n4. In the greedy scheduler, when multiple ops are ready at the same time on different machines, I schedule them all. But what if two ops from DIFFERENT jobs are ready at the same time on the same machine? My greedy handles this by picking the one with best priority (MWKR) and skipping the other (usedM).\n\nBut after the iteration, the skipped op doesn\'t appear in the next iteration until `max(machFree[m], jobReady[j])` equals the NEXT time t.
